class="postdate"></div>     <h3><span class="itmRating"><img class="eggs r4" alt="4 out of 5 eggs" src="http://images10.newegg.com/WebResource/Themes/2005/Nest/none.gif" /><span class="print" style="display:none;">Rating: 4/5</span></span>Software shadow copy issues</h3>    <div class="details">                      <div class="review-title" ><p><strong>This review is from: </strong>SAMSUNG 840 EVO MZ-7TE1T0BW 2.5" 1TB SATA III MLC Internal Solid State Drive (SSD)                                                                                                                                                              </p></div>                                      <p><em>Pros:</em> Finally SSD are getting to size that we can have them for a solo disk on a computer.  Very quick, silent.   Some neat software which can allow RAM disks if you have tons of memory - nothing like seeing &#62; 4000 mb&#47;sec rates.  Transfers of files easily saturate my GB NIC while using &#60; 5&#37; processor, amazing.</p>     <p><em>Cons:</em> Ever since I installed the software from Samsung I can no longer use Microsoft backup software as it fails to use VSS &#40;shadow copy&#41; in Windows 7 pro.  I can&#39;t find this on any forums.  I have it turned on in services.  My backup locks at 7&#37; complete.  Some of the files are large &#62; 150 GB</p>          <p><em>Other Thoughts:</em> I am so happy SSD are finally at point were I don&#39;t need to buy them in piles then put them into a RAID to get useful size and speed.  In long run this is cheaper for me.  I have these running on a couple of computers.  VSS issues seen on all of these.  I don&#39;t have issues with other HDD and and other branded SSD so this is unique problem to Samsung disked computers only.  I am backing up to FreeNAS based unit over CIFS but it also fails over backup to iSCSI based disk.  I can easily and quickly manually backup the files essential but I would love to have it automated as before.</p>       <blockquote>     <em>Manufacturer Response:</em><p>Jim R.&#58;  <br><br>Thank you for purchasing the Samsung 840 EVO Series SSD.<br><br>I am sorry to hear that you are having difficulties with Microsft backup software.<br><br>To better assist you with step-by-step troubleshooting, please contact Samsung Customer Support toll-free at 1-800-SAMSUNG and a representative will gladly help you.  Support hours are from 9AM to 9PM EST, Monday through Friday.     </p> </blockquote>     </div>         <p class="helpful">      1 out of 1 people found this review helpful. <span id="dyu4168104"> Did class="itmRating"><img class="eggs r1" alt="1 out of 5 eggs" src="http://images10.newegg.com/WebResource/Themes/2005/Nest/none.gif" /><span class="print" style="display:none;">Rating: 1/5</span></span>Warning, TLC&#47;FW bug</h3>    <div class="details">                      <div class="review-title" ><p><strong>This review is from: </strong>SAMSUNG 840 EVO MZ-7TE1T0BW 2.5" 1TB SATA III MLC Internal Solid State Drive (SSD)                                                                                                                                                              </p></div>                                      <p><em>Pros:</em> Samsung flooded the market with these drives which helped bring down SSD prices.</p>     <p><em>Cons:</em> Firmware bug will bring your OS to a screeching halt after a few months.  I have two 250GB, five 500GB and one 1TB drives and it has taken me several hours to go through all of them.</p>          <p><em>Other Thoughts:</em> Samsung is very quietly acknowledging an ugly firmware bug &#40;or flaw in their TLC flash&#41; that renders ALL 840 EVO drives virtually worthless when reading data that is a few months old.  If you don&#39;t run their cheesy FW updating program, any data such as important Windows OS files that get read every time you run your PC will slow to as low as 20MBs read speeds.  I have 8 of these drives &#40;a &#36;2K investment&#41; that all have the same problem.  When you run their FW fix program you may loose all your data.  If you buy one new I suggest you do it BEFORE you put it into service.  Otherwise you should do a full image backup, FW fix, then reimage the drive.  Nobody knows if the FW fix will work in the long term either.  Google it and HD Tach and you will see what I mean.  I will never buy another Samsung drive again.</p>         </div>         <p class="helpful">      7 out of 7 people found this review helpful. <span id="dyu4161872"> Did you?</span> <span
